The form of vertical farming that uses aquatic plants to grow crops is known as Aquaponics. In this system, fish and plants are grown together in a symbiotic environment. The waste produced by the fish provides an organic nutrient source for the plants, while the plants help to filter and clean the water, which is then recirculated back to the fish tanks. This closed-loop system allows for efficient use of resources and can be highly productive in terms of crop yield per square foot compared to traditional soil farming methods. Aquaponics combines aquaculture (raising aquatic animals) and hydroponics (cultivating plants in water without soil) into one integrated system, often used for growing leafy greens like lettuce, as well as herbs and other vegetables that thrive in such conditions.
